**TASK DESCRIPTION:**
# Gzip Compression Task

## Description

This task involves compressing a given block of binary data using the standard gzip compression algorithm. The input data is generated using a Zipfian distribution of words.

The key requirements for a valid solution are:
1.  The compressed data, when decompressed, must exactly match the original input data.
2.  The size (length in bytes) of the compressed data produced by the solution must be less than or equal to the size produced by the reference `solve()` method (which uses deterministic compression).

## Input

A dictionary containing:
- `plaintext`: A `bytes` object representing the data to be compressed.

## Output

A dictionary containing:
- `compressed_data`: A `bytes` object representing the gzip-compressed data.

Category: misc


Below is the reference implementation. Your function should run much quicker.

import gzip
import math  # Added for ceiling function
import string  # Needed for random word generation
from typing import Any
import numpy as np

| 01: def is_solution( problem: dict[str, Any], solution: dict[str, bytes] | Any) -> bool:
| 02:     """
| 03:     Verify the provided gzip compression solution.
| 04: 
| 05:     Checks:
| 06:     1. The solution format is valid (dict with 'compressed_data' as bytes).
| 07:     2. Decompressing the solution's data yields the original plaintext.
| 08:     3. The length of the compressed data in the solution is at most
| 09:        machine epsilon larger than the length produced by solve().
| 10: 
| 11:     Args:
| 12:         problem (dict): The problem dictionary.
| 13:         solution (dict): The proposed solution dictionary with 'compressed_data'.
| 14: 
| 15:     Returns:
| 16:         bool: True if the solution is valid and meets the criteria.
| 17:     """
| 18:     if not isinstance(solution, dict) or "compressed_data" not in solution:
| 19:         logging.error(
| 20:             f"Invalid solution format. Expected dict with 'compressed_data'. Got: {type(solution)}"
| 21:         )
| 22:         return False
| 23: 
| 24:     compressed_data = solution["compressed_data"]
| 25:     if not isinstance(compressed_data, bytes):
| 26:         logging.error("Solution 'compressed_data' is not bytes.")
| 27:         return False
| 28: 
| 29:     original_plaintext = problem.get("plaintext")
| 30:     if original_plaintext is None:
| 31:         logging.error("Problem dictionary missing 'plaintext'. Cannot verify.")
| 32:         return False  # Cannot verify without original data
| 33: 
| 34:     # 1. Check if decompression yields the original input
| 35:     try:
| 36:         decompressed_data = gzip.decompress(compressed_data)
| 37:     except Exception as e:
| 38:         logging.error(f"Failed to decompress solution data: {e}")
| 39:         return False
| 40: 
| 41:     if decompressed_data != original_plaintext:
| 42:         logging.error("Decompressed data does not match original plaintext.")
| 43:         # Log lengths for debugging
| 44:         logging.debug(
| 45:             f"Original length: {len(original_plaintext)}, Decompressed length: {len(decompressed_data)}"
| 46:         )
| 47:         # Log first/last few bytes if lengths match but content differs
| 48:         if len(decompressed_data) == len(original_plaintext):
| 49:             logging.debug(
| 50:                 f"Original start: {original_plaintext[:50]}, Decompressed start: {decompressed_data[:50]}"
| 51:             )
| 52:             logging.debug(
| 53:                 f"Original end: {original_plaintext[-50:]}, Decompressed end: {decompressed_data[-50:]}"
| 54:             )
| 55:         return False
| 56: 
| 57:     # 2. Check if the compressed size is close to the reference solution size
| 58:     #    Generate reference solution using the same compression settings.
| 59:     try:
| 60:         # reference_solution = solve(problem) # Use direct compression here to avoid recursion if solve changes
| 61:         reference_compressed_data = gzip.compress(original_plaintext, compresslevel=9, mtime=0)
| 62:     except Exception as e:
| 63:         logging.error(f"Failed to generate reference solution in is_solution: {e}")
| 64:         # Cannot verify size constraint if reference generation fails
| 65:         return False
| 66: 
| 67:     solution_len = len(compressed_data)
| 68:     reference_len = len(reference_compressed_data)
| 69: 
| 70:     # Allow solution length to be at most 0.1% larger than reference length.
| 71:     # Calculate the maximum allowed length (reference + 0.1%)
| 72:     # Use math.ceil to allow the integer length to reach the ceiling of the limit.
| 73:     max_allowed_len = math.ceil(reference_len * 1.001)
| 74: 
| 75:     # Calculate compression ratios for logging
| 76:     # original_len = len(original_plaintext)
| 77:     # Avoid division by zero if original_plaintext is empty
| 78:     # ref_ratio = (reference_len / original_len) if original_len > 0 else float('inf')
| 79:     # sol_ratio = (solution_len / original_len) if original_len > 0 else float('inf')
| 80: 
| 81: 
| 82:     if solution_len > max_allowed_len:
| 83:         logging.error(
| 84:             f"Compressed data length ({solution_len}) is more than 0.1% larger than reference length ({reference_len}). Max allowed: {max_allowed_len}."
| 85:         )
| 86:         return False
| 87: 
| 88:     # All checks passed
| 89:     return True

AlgoTune Task Description 
# Gzip Compression Task

## Description

This task involves compressing a given block of binary data using the standard gzip compression algorithm. The input data is generated using a Zipfian distribution of words.

The key requirements for a valid solution are:
1.  The compressed data, when decompressed, must exactly match the original input data.
2.  The size (length in bytes) of the compressed data produced by the solution must be less than or equal to the size produced by the reference `solve()` method (which uses deterministic compression).

## Input

A dictionary containing:
- `plaintext`: A `bytes` object representing the data to be compressed.

## Output

A dictionary containing:
- `compressed_data`: A `bytes` object representing the gzip-compressed data.

Category: misc
Reference Implementation 
import gzip
import math  # Added for ceiling function
import string  # Needed for random word generation
from typing import Any
import numpy as np

 def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
     """
     Compress the plaintext using the gzip algorithm with mtime=0.
 
     Args:
         problem (dict): The problem dictionary generated by `generate_problem`.
 
     Returns:
         dict: A dictionary containing 'compressed_data'.
     
 
     NOTE: Your solution must pass validation by:
     1. Returning correctly formatted output
     2. Having no NaN or infinity values
     3. Matching expected results within numerical tolerance
     """
     plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
 
     try:
         # Compress the data using gzip, setting compresslevel=9 and mtime=0 for deterministic output
         compressed_data = gzip.compress(plaintext, compresslevel=9, mtime=0)
         return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
 
     except Exception as e:
         raise  # Re-raise exception
Best AlgoTuner-Generated Code
solver.py
import gzip

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use compression level 9 to match reference size constraints
        compressed_data = gzip.compress(plaintext, compresslevel=9, mtime=0)
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

Language Model Invalid Command
Let's start by creating the initial solver implementation. The reference solution uses gzip.compress with level 9, which is slow for large inputs. We can potentially improve performance by using zlib directly with a faster compression level while maintaining the required gzip format and deterministic output.

The plan:
1. Use zlib.compressobj with wbits=31 to produce gzip-formatted output
2. Set compression level to 6 for better speed/size balance
3. Ensure mtime=0 by not setting it (defaults to 0)
4. Return compressed data in same format as reference

Here's the implementation:<｜tool▁calls▁begin｜><｜tool▁call▁begin｜>function<｜tool▁sep｜>edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-0
---
import zlib
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Use zlib with gzip wrapper (wbits=31) for faster compression
compressor = zlib.compressobj(level=6, wbits=31)
compressed_data = compressor.compress(plaintext)
compressed_data += compressor.flush()
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
---

- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---
def improved_function():
print("Optimized solution")
---
- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

import zlib
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Use zlib with gzip wrapper (wbits=31) for faster compression
# Set compression level to 6 for better speed/size balance
compressor = zlib.compressobj(level=6, wbits=31)
compressed_data = compressor.compress(plaintext)
compressed_data += compressor.flush()
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

import gzip
from typing import Any

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use balanced compression level (6) for better speed/compression ratio
        compressed_data = gzip.compress(plaintext, compresslevel=6, mtime=0)
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

Let me create the solver.py file with the correct command syntax:<｜tool▁calls▁begin｜><｜tool▁call▁begin｜>function<｜tool▁sep｜>edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-9
---
import zlib
import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Manually create gzip format with zlib for better performance
# Header: magic (2) + method (1) + flags (1) + mtime (4) + extra flags (1) + os (1)
header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
# Compress with zlib using maximum speed strategy
compressor = zlib.compressobj(
level=zlib.Z_BEST_SPEED,
method=zlib.DEFLATED,
wbits=-zlib.MAX_WBITS, # Negative for raw deflate stream
strategy=zlib.Z_HUFFMAN_ONLY
)
compressed = compressor.compress(plaintext) + compressor.flush()
# Calculate CRC and length
crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext)
size = len(plaintext)
# Footer: CRC (4) + uncompressed size (4)
footer = struct.pack("<I", crc) + struct.pack("<I", size & 0xffffffff)
compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
---

file: solver.py
lines: 1-10
---
import zlib
import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
# Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)
# Calculate CRC32 and original size
crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
size = len(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
# Build footer: CRC32 and ISIZE (original size mod 2^32)
footer = struct.pack("<II", crc, size)
compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
---

- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

import zlib
import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
# Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)
# Calculate CRC32 and original size
crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
size = len(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
# Build footer: CRC32 and ISIZE (original size mod 2^32)
footer = struct.pack("<II", crc, size)
compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
---

- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).

```

import zlib
import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
# Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)
# Calculate CRC32 and original size
crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
size = len(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
# Build footer: CRC32 and ISIZE (original size mod 2^32)
footer = struct.pack("<II", crc, size)
compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```

```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.

Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```

Example:

import zlib
import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
# Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)
# Calculate CRC32 and original size
crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
size = len(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
# Build footer: CRC32 and ISIZE (original size mod 2^32)
footer = struct.pack("<II", crc, size)
compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
# Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)

Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]

import zlib
import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
# Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)
# Calculate CRC32 and original size
crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
size = len(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
# Build footer: CRC32 and ISIZE (original size mod 2^32)
footer = struct.pack("<II", crc, size)
compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
# Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
# Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)
# Calculate CRC32 and original size
crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
size = len(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
# Build footer: CRC32 and ISIZE (original size mod 2^32)
footer = struct.pack("<II", crc, size)
compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
---

- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.

```
delete
file: <file_name>

lines: 5-10

- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```

import zlib
import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
        header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
        # Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
        compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)
        # Calculate CRC32 and original size
        crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
        size = len(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
        # Build footer: CRC32 and ISIZE (original size mod 2^32)
        footer = struct.pack("<II", crc, size)
        compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

import zlib
import struct
from typing import Any

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, bytes]:
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Build gzip header: magic, compression method, flags, mtime, extra flags, OS
        header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
        # Compress with zlib in raw mode (wbits=-15) at level 9
        compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=9, wbits=-15)
        # Calculate CRC32 and original size
        crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
        size = len(plaintext) & 0xffffffff
        # Build footer: CRC32 and ISIZE (original size mod 2^32)
        footer = struct.pack("<II", crc, size)
        compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

```

edit
file: solver.py

import zlib
import gzip
import io

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        
        # Compress with zlib at level 1 for speed
        compressed = zlib.compress(plaintext, level=1)
        
        # Create gzip wrapper
        with io.BytesIO() as f:
            with gzip.GzipFile(fileobj=f, mode='w', mtime=0) as gz:
                gz.write(plaintext)
            compressed_data = f.getvalue()
            
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
---

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>

```

file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

import gzip

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use compression level 1 for faster compression
        compressed_data = gzip.compress(plaintext, compresslevel=1, mtime=0)
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

class Solver:

import gzip

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use compression level 6 for a good balance of speed and compression ratio
        compressed_data = gzip.compress(plaintext, compresslevel=6, mtime=0)
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The evaluation shows our implementation is correct but not optimized enough. Let's try using zlib directly with a faster compression level and strategy while still meeting the size constraints. We'll implement manual gzip formatting to ensure compatibility.

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-8
---
import zlib
import struct

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use faster compression level with Huffman-only strategy
        crc = zlib.crc32(plaintext)
        size = len(plaintext)
        # Level 4 with Z_HUFFMAN_ONLY strategy for speed
        compressor = zlib.compressobj(
            level=4,
            method=zlib.DEFLATED,
            wbits=-15,  # Negative wbits for raw deflate
            strategy=zlib.Z_HUFFMAN_ONLY
        )
        compressed = compressor.compress(plaintext)
        compressed += compressor.flush()
        
        # Build gzip format manually: header + compressed + footer
        header = b'\x1f\x8b\x08\x00\x00\x00\x00\x00\x02\xff'
        footer = struct.pack("<I", crc) + struct.pack("<I", size & 0xffffffff)
        compressed_data = header + compressed + footer
        
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
---

Here are the commands available to you. Ensure you include one and only one of the following commands in each of your responses:
- `edit`: Replace a range of lines with new content in a file. This is how you can create files: if the file does not exist, it will be created. Here is an example:
```
edit
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---
def improved_function():
print("Optimized solution")
---
- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

lines: <start_line>-<end_line>
---
<new_content>
---
```

The command will:
1. Delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)
2. Insert <new_content> starting at <start_line>
3. If both <start_line> and <end_line> are 0, <new_content> will be prepended to the file

Example:
edit
file: solver.py
lines: 5-7
---
def improved_function():
print("Optimized solution")
---
- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the issue. The current implementation is manually building the gzip header and footer, but there's a problem with the header format. Let's fix it by using the standard `gzip` module with a faster compression level that still produces acceptable compression size.

The reference solution uses level 9 which is slow. We can use level 6 which is faster while still providing good compression. According to zlib documentation, level 6 is the default and offers a good balance between speed and compression ratio.

Here's the optimized implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 1-25
---
import gzip

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Use faster compression level (6) that still provides good compression
        # while being significantly faster than level 9
        compressed_data = gzip.compress(plaintext, compresslevel=6, mtime=0)
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
---

- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

- `ls`: List all files in the current working directory.
- `view_file <file_name> [start_line]`: Display 100 lines of `<file_name>` starting from `start_line` (defaults to line 1).
- `revert`: Revert the code to the best-performing version thus far.
- `reference <string>`: Query the reference solver with a problem and receive its solution. If the problem's input is a list, this command would look like:
```
reference [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval_input <string>`: Run your current solver implementation on the given input. This is the only command that shows stdout from your solver along with both solutions. Example:
```
eval_input [1,2,3,4]
```
- `eval`: Run evaluation on the current solution and report the results.
- `delete`: Delete a range of lines from a file using the format:
```
delete
file: <file_name>
lines: <start_line>-<end_line>

The command will delete the lines from <start_line> to <end_line> (inclusive)

Example:
```
delete
file: solver.py
lines: 5-10
```
- `profile <filename.py> <input>`: Profile your currently loaded solve method's performance on a given input. Shows the 25 most time-consuming lines. Requires specifying a python file (e.g., `solver.py`) for validation, though profiling runs on the current in-memory code.
Example:
```
profile solver.py [1, 2, 3]
```
- `profile_lines <filename.py> <line_number1, line_number2, ...> <input>`: Profiles the chosen lines of the currently loaded code on the given input. Requires specifying a python file for validation.
Example:
```
profile_lines solver.py 1,2,3 [1, 2, 3]
```

import gzip

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem, **kwargs):
        plaintext = problem["plaintext"]
        # Using compression level 1 for maximum speed
        compressed_data = gzip.compress(plaintext, compresslevel=1, mtime=0)
        return {"compressed_data": compressed_data}
